<ul><li><img alt="icon" class="noviewer" data-file-height="250" data-file-width="107" decoding="async" height="16" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/WHO_Rod.svg/7px-WHO_Rod.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/WHO_Rod.svg/10px-WHO_Rod.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/WHO_Rod.svg/13px-WHO_Rod.svg.png 2x" width="7"/> <a href="/wiki/Portal:Medicine" title="Portal:Medicine">Medicine portal</a></li>

portal</a></li></ul></td></tr><tr><td class="sidebar-navbar"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1063604349">.mw-parser-output .navbar{display:inline;font-size:88%;font-weight:normal}.mw-parser-output .navbar-collapse{float:left;text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .navbar-boxtext{word-spacing:0}.mw-parser-output .navbar ul{display:inline-block;white-space:nowrap;line-height:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::before{margin-right:-0.125em;content:"[ "}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::after{margin-left:-0.125em;content:" ]"}.mw-parser-output .navbar li{word-spacing:-0.125em}.mw-parser-output .navbar a>span,.mw-parser-output .navbar a>abbr{text-decoration:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-mini abbr{font-variant:small-caps;border-bottom:none;text-decoration:none;cursor:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-full{font-size:114%;margin:0 7em}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-mini{font-size:114%;margin:0 4em}</style><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Public_health_sidebar" title="Template:Public health sidebar"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Public_health_sidebar" title="Template talk:Public health sidebar"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Public_health_sidebar&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Mental health</b> encompasses emotional, psychological, and social well-being. It influences <a href="/wiki/Cognition" title="Cognition">cognition</a>, <a href="/wiki/Perception" title="Perception">perception</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Behavior" title="Behavior">behavior</a>. It also determines how an individual handles <a href="/wiki/Stress_(biology)" title="Stress (biology)">stress</a>, <a href="/wiki/Interpersonal_relationship" title="Interpersonal relationship">interpersonal relationships</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Decision-making" title="Decision-making">decision-making</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:10_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-:10-1">[1]</a></sup> Mental health includes subjective well-being, perceived <a href="/wiki/Self-efficacy" title="Self-efficacy">self-efficacy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Autonomy" title="Autonomy">autonomy</a>, competence, intergenerational dependence, and self-actualization of one's intellectual and emotional potential, among others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-WHO-2">[2]</a></sup> From the perspectives of <a href="/wiki/Positive_psychology" title="Positive psychology">positive psychology</a> or <a href="/wiki/Holism" title="Holism">holism</a>, mental health may include an individual's ability to enjoy life and to create a balance between life activities and efforts to achieve <a href="/wiki/Psychological_resilience" title="Psychological resilience">psychological resilience</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> Cultural differences, subjective assessments, and competing professional theories all affect how one defines "mental health".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> Some early signs related to mental health problems are sleep irritation, lack of energy and thinking of harming yourself or others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup>
</p>
<div aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading" class="toc" id="toc" role="navigation"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" lang="en"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Mental_disorders">Mental disorders</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mental_health&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Mental disorders">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Mental_disorder" title="Mental disorder">Mental disorder</a></div>
<p>Mental health, as <b>defined</b> by the <a href="/wiki/Public_Health_Agency_of_Canada" title="Public Health Agency of Canada">Public Health Agency of Canada</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> is an individual's capacity to feel, think, and act in ways to achieve a better quality of life while respecting the personal, social, and cultural boundaries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Manwell_e007079_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Manwell_e007079-7">[7]</a></sup> Impairment of any of these are risk factors for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mental_disorders" title="Mental disorders">mental disorders</a>, or mental illness <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> which is a component of mental health.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Manwell_e007079_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-Manwell_e007079-7">[7]</a></sup> Mental disorders are defined as the health conditions that affect and alter cognitive functioning, emotional responses, and behavior associated with distress and/or impaired functioning.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/ICD-11" title="ICD-11">ICD-11</a> is the global standard used to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diagnose" title="Diagnose">diagnose</a>, treat, research, and report various mental disorders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> In the United States, the <a href="/wiki/DSM-5" title="DSM-5">DSM-5</a> is used as the classification system of mental disorders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Regier_92–98_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-Regier_92–98-13">[13]</a></sup>
</p><p>Mental health is associated with a number of lifestyle factors such as diet, exercise, stress, drug abuse, social connections and interactions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Regier_92–98_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-Regier_92–98-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> Therapists, psychiatrists, psychologists, social workers, nurse practitioners, or family physicians can help manage mental illness with treatments such as therapy, counseling or <a href="/wiki/Medication" title="Medication">medication</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mental_health&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Well-being" title="Well-being">Well-being</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eudaimonia" title="Eudaimonia">Eudaimonia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/History_of_mental_disorders" title="History of mental disorders">History of mental disorders</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mental_health&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the mid-19th century, William Sweetser was the first to coin the term <i>mental hygiene</i>, which can be seen as the precursor to contemporary approaches to work on promoting positive mental health.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mandell1995_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mandell1995-17">[17]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Ray" title="Isaac Ray">Isaac Ray</a>, the fourth president<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> of the <a href="/wiki/American_Psychiatric_Association" title="American Psychiatric Association">American Psychiatric Association</a> and one of its founders, further defined mental hygiene as "the art of preserving the mind against all incidents and influences calculated to deteriorate its qualities, impair its energies, or derange its movements".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mandell1995_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-Mandell1995-17">[17]</a></sup>
</p><p>In American history, mentally ill patients were thought to be religiously punished. This response persisted through the 1700s, along with the inhumane confinement and stigmatization of such individuals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-:3-19">[19]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dorothea_Dix" title="Dorothea Dix">Dorothea Dix</a> (1802–1887) was an important figure in the development of the "mental hygiene" movement. Dix was a school teacher who endeavored to help people with mental disorders and to expose the sub-standard conditions into which they were put.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barlow1_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-Barlow1-20">[20]</a></sup> This became known as the "mental hygiene movement".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barlow1_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-Barlow1-20">[20]</a></sup> Before this movement, it was not uncommon that people affected by mental illness would be considerably neglected, often left alone in deplorable conditions without sufficient clothing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barlow1_20-2"><a href="#cite_note-Barlow1-20">[20]</a></sup> From 1840 to 1880, she won the support of the federal government to set up over 30 state psychiatric hospitals; however, they were understaffed, under-resourced, and were accused of violating <a href="/wiki/Human_rights" title="Human rights">human rights</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-:3-19">[19]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Emil_Kraepelin" title="Emil Kraepelin">Emil Kraepelin</a> in 1896 developed the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taxonomy_(general)" title="Taxonomy (general)">taxonomy</a> of mental disorders which has dominated the field for nearly 80 years. Later, the proposed disease model of abnormality was subjected to analysis and considered normality to be relative to the physical, geographical and cultural aspects of the defining group.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup>
</p><p>At the beginning of the 20th century, <a href="/wiki/Clifford_Whittingham_Beers" title="Clifford Whittingham Beers">Clifford Beers</a> founded "Mental Health America – National Committee for Mental Hygiene", after publication of his accounts as a patient in several <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lunatic_asylums" title="Lunatic asylums">lunatic asylums</a>, <i>A Mind That Found Itself</i>, in 1908<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CliffordBeersClinic_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-CliffordBeersClinic-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_roots_of_the_concept_of_mental_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_roots_of_the_concept_of_mental-24">[24]</a></sup> and opened the first outpatient mental health <a href="/wiki/Clinic" title="Clinic">clinic</a> in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CliffordBeersClinic_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-CliffordBeersClinic-23">[23]</a></sup>
</p><p>The mental hygiene movement, similar to the <a href="/wiki/Social_hygiene_movement" title="Social hygiene movement">social hygiene movement</a>, had at times been associated with advocating <a href="/wiki/Eugenics" title="Eugenics">eugenics</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sterilisation_(medicine)" title="Sterilisation (medicine)">sterilization</a> of those considered too mentally deficient to be assisted into productive work and contented family life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> In the post-WWII years, references to mental hygiene were gradually replaced by the term 'mental health' due to its positive aspect that evolves from the treatment of illness to preventive and promotive areas of healthcare.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_roots_of_the_concept_of_mental_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-The_roots_of_the_concept_of_mental-24">[24]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Deinstitutionalization_and_transinstitutionalization">Deinstitutionalization and transinstitutionalization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mental_health&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Deinstitutionalization and transinstitutionalization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>When state hospitals were accused of violating human rights, advocates pushed for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deinstitutionalization" title="Deinstitutionalization">deinstitutionalization</a>: the replacement of federal mental hospitals for <a href="/wiki/Community_mental_health_service" title="Community mental health service">community mental health services</a>. The closure of state-provisioned psychiatric hospitals was enforced by the Community Mental Health Centers Act in 1963 that laid out terms in which only patients who posed an imminent danger to others or themselves could be admitted into state facilities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> This was seen as an improvement from previous conditions. However, there remains a debate on the conditions of these community resources.
</p><p>It has been proven that this transition was beneficial for many patients: there was an increase in overall satisfaction, a better quality of life, and more friendships between patients, and not too costly. This proved to be true only in the circumstance that treatment facilities that had enough funding for staff and equipment as well as proper management.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> However, this idea is a polarizing issue. Critics of deinstitutionalization argue that poor living conditions prevailed, patients were lonely, and they did not acquire proper medical care in these treatment homes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-:4-29">[29]</a></sup> Additionally, patients that were moved from state psychiatric care to nursing and residential homes had deficits in crucial aspects of their treatment. Some cases result in the shift of care from health workers to patients' families, where they do not have the proper funding or medical expertise to give proper care.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-:4-29">[29]</a></sup> On the other hand, patients that are treated in community mental health centers lack sufficient cancer testing, <a href="/wiki/Vaccination" title="Vaccination">vaccinations</a>, or otherwise regular medical check-ups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_29-2"><a href="#cite_note-:4-29">[29]</a></sup>
</p><p>Other critics of state deinstitutionalization argue that this was simply a transition to "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transinstitutionalization" title="Transinstitutionalization">transinstitutionalization</a>", or the idea that prisons and state-provisioned hospitals are interdependent. In other words, patients become inmates. This draws on the Penrose Hypothesis of 1939, which theorized that there was an inverse relationship between prisons' population size and the number of psychiatric hospital beds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:5_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-:5-30">[30]</a></sup> This means that populations that require psychiatric mental care will transition between institutions, which in this case, includes state psychiatric hospitals and criminal justice systems. Thus, a decrease in available psychiatric hospital beds occurred at the same time as an increase in inmates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:5_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-:5-30">[30]</a></sup> Although some are skeptical that this is due to other external factors, others will reason this conclusion to a lack of empathy for the mentally ill. There is no argument in the social stigmatization of those with mental illnesses, they have been widely marginalized and discriminated against in society.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_19-2"><a href="#cite_note-:3-19">[19]</a></sup> In this source, researchers analyze how most compensation prisoners (detainees who are unable or unwilling to pay a fine for petty crimes) are unemployed, homeless, and with an extraordinarily high degree of mental illnesses and <a href="/wiki/Substance_use_disorder" title="Substance use disorder">substance use disorders</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:5_30-2"><a href="#cite_note-:5-30">[30]</a></sup> Compensation prisoners then lose prospective job opportunities, face social marginalization, and lack access to resocialization programs, which ultimately facilitate reoffending.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:5_30-3"><a href="#cite_note-:5-30">[30]</a></sup> The research sheds light on how the mentally ill—and in this case, the poor—are further punished for certain circumstances that are beyond their control, and that this is a vicious cycle that repeats itself. Thus, prisons embody another state-provisioned mental hospital.
</p><p>Families of patients, advocates, and mental health professionals still call for the increase in more well-structured community facilities and treatment programs with a higher quality of long-term inpatient resources and care. With this more structured environment, the United States will continue with more access to mental health care and an increase in the overall treatment of the mentally ill.
</p><p>However, there is still a lack of studies for mental health conditions (MHCs) to raise awareness, knowledge development, and attitude of seeking medical treatment for MHCs in Bangladesh. People in rural areas often seek treatment from the traditional healers and MHCs are sometimes considered a spiritual matter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Epidemiology">Epidemiology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mental_health&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Epidemiology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Epidemiology" title="Epidemiology">Epidemiology</a></div>
<p>Mental illnesses are more common than <a href="/wiki/Cancer" title="Cancer">cancer</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diabetes_mellitus" title="Diabetes mellitus">diabetes</a>, or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heart_disease" title="Heart disease">heart disease</a>. Over 26 percent of all Americans over the age of 18 meet the criteria for having a mental illness.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> Evidence suggests that 450 million people worldwide have some mental illness. <a href="/wiki/Major_depressive_disorder" title="Major depressive disorder">Major depression</a> ranks fourth among the top 10 leading causes of disease worldwide. By 2029, mental illness is predicted to become the leading cause of disease worldwide. One million people commit suicide every year and 10 to 20 million attempt it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> (WHO) report estimates the global cost of mental illness at nearly $2.5 trillion (two-thirds in indirect costs) in 2010, with a projected increase to over $6 trillion by 2030.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup>
</p><p>Evidence from the WHO suggests that nearly half of the world's population is affected by mental illness with an impact on their <a href="/wiki/Self-esteem" title="Self-esteem">self-esteem</a>, relationships and ability to function in everyday life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> An individual's emotional health can impact their physical health. Poor mental health can lead to problems such as the inability to make adequate decisions and <a href="/wiki/Substance_use_disorder" title="Substance use disorder">substance use disorders</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Richards_2010_247_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-Richards_2010_247-36">[36]</a></sup>
</p><p>Good mental health can improve life quality whereas poor mental health can worsen it. According to Richards, Campania, &amp; Muse-Burke, "There is growing evidence that is showing emotional abilities are associated with pro-social behaviors such as stress management and physical health."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Richards_2010_247_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-Richards_2010_247-36">[36]</a></sup> Their research also concluded that people who lack emotional expression are inclined to anti-social behaviors (e.g., substance use disorder and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alcohol_use_disorder" title="Alcohol use disorder">alcohol use disorder</a>, physical fights, <a href="/wiki/Vandalism" title="Vandalism">vandalism</a>), which reflects one's mental health and suppressed emotions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Richards_2010_247_36-2"><a href="#cite_note-Richards_2010_247-36">[36]</a></sup> Adults and children who face mental illness may experience <a href="/wiki/Social_stigma" title="Social stigma">social stigma</a>, which can exacerbate the issues.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Global_prevalence">Global prevalence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mental_health&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Global prevalence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Global_mental_health" title="Global mental health">Global mental health</a> and <a href="/wiki/Category:Mental_health_by_country" title="Category:Mental health by country">Category:Mental health by country</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Two_Continua_Model_Large.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4500" data-file-width="4500" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Two_Continua_Model_Large.png/220px-Two_Continua_Model_Large.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Two_Continua_Model_Large.png/330px-Two_Continua_Model_Large.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Two_Continua_Model_Large.png/440px-Two_Continua_Model_Large.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Two_Continua_Model_Large.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Two Continua Model of Mental Health and Mental Illness</div></div></div>
<p>Mental health can be seen as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Continuum_(theory)" title="Continuum (theory)">continuum</a>, where an individual's mental health may have many different possible <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Value_(ethics)" title="Value (ethics)">values</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Keyes2002_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-Keyes2002-38">[38]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Well-being" title="Well-being">Mental wellness</a> is viewed as a positive attribute; this definition of mental health highlights <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Emotional_well-being" title="Emotional well-being">emotional well-being</a>, the capacity to live a full and <a href="/wiki/Creativity" title="Creativity">creative</a> life, and the flexibility to deal with life's inevitable challenges. Some discussions are formulated in terms of contentment or happiness.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> Many therapeutic systems and self-help books offer methods and philosophies espousing strategies and techniques vaunted as effective for further improving the mental wellness. <a href="/wiki/Positive_psychology" title="Positive psychology">Positive psychology</a> is increasingly prominent in mental health.
</p><p>A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Holistic" title="Holistic">holistic</a> model of mental health generally includes concepts based upon <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anthropological" title="Anthropological">anthropological</a>, <a href="/wiki/Education" title="Education">educational</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Psychological" title="Psychological">psychological</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Religious" title="Religious">religious</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sociological" title="Sociological">sociological</a> perspectives. There are also models as theoretical perspectives from <a href="/wiki/Personality_psychology" title="Personality psychology">personality</a>, <a href="/wiki/Social_psychology" title="Social psychology">social</a>, <a href="/wiki/Clinical_psychology" title="Clinical psychology">clinical</a>, <a href="/wiki/Health_psychology" title="Health psychology">health</a> and <a href="/wiki/Developmental_psychology" title="Developmental psychology">developmental psychology</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WitmerSweeney_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-WitmerSweeney-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HattieMyersSweeney_p354364_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-HattieMyersSweeney_p354364-41">[41]</a></sup>
</p><p>The tripartite model of mental well-being<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Keyes2002_38-1"><a href="#cite_note-Keyes2002-38">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-42">[42]</a></sup> views mental well-being as encompassing three components of emotional well-being, social well-being, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Psychological_well-being" title="Psychological well-being">psychological well-being</a>. Emotional well-being is defined as having high levels of positive emotions, whereas social and psychological well-being are defined as the presence of psychological and social skills and abilities that contribute to optimal functioning in daily life. The model has received empirical support across cultures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_42-1"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-42">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> The Mental Health Continuum-Short Form (MHC-SF) is the most widely used scale to measure the tripartite model of mental well-being.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mental_health&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Children_and_young_adults">Children and young adults</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mental_health&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Children and young adults">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Infant_mental_health" title="Infant mental health">Infant mental health</a> and <a href="/wiki/Child_and_Adolescent_Mental_Health" title="Child and Adolescent Mental Health">Child and Adolescent Mental Health</a></div><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Depression_in_childhood_and_adolescence" title="Depression in childhood and adolescence">Depression in childhood and adolescence</a></div>
<p>Mental health conditions are 16% of the global burden of disease and injury in people aged 10–19 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-:1-48">[48]</a></sup>  8.9 million dead children. 42% of those young adults went untreated as of 2018.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:10_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-:10-1">[1]</a></sup> Half of all mental health conditions start by 14 years of age but most cases go undetected and untreated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_48-1"><a href="#cite_note-:1-48">[48]</a></sup> Depression is one of the leading causes of illness and disability among adolescents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_48-2"><a href="#cite_note-:1-48">[48]</a></sup> Suicide is the fourth leading cause of death in 15-19-year-olds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_48-3"><a href="#cite_note-:1-48">[48]</a></sup> Exposure to childhood trauma can cause mental health disorders and poor academic achievement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> Ignoring mental health conditions in adolescents can impact adulthood.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-:2-51">[51]</a></sup> 50% of preschool children show a natural reduction in behavioral problems. The remaining experience long-term consequences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_51-1"><a href="#cite_note-:2-51">[51]</a></sup> It impairs physical and mental health and limits opportunities to live fulfilling lives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_51-2"><a href="#cite_note-:2-51">[51]</a></sup> A result of depression during adolescence and adulthood may be substance abuse.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_51-3"><a href="#cite_note-:2-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:6_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-:6-52">[52]</a></sup> The average age of onset is between 11 and 14 years for depressive disorders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:6_52-1"><a href="#cite_note-:6-52">[52]</a></sup> Only approximately 25% of children with behavioral problems refer to medical services.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_51-4"><a href="#cite_note-:2-51">[51]</a></sup> The majority of children go to die.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_51-5"><a href="#cite_note-:2-51">[51]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Homeless_population">Homeless population</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mental_health&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Homeless population">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Homelessness_and_mental_health" title="Homelessness and mental health">Homelessness and mental health</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:255px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Homeless_woman_sitting.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1848" data-file-width="2499" decoding="async" height="187" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Homeless_woman_sitting.jpg/253px-Homeless_woman_sitting.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Homeless_woman_sitting.jpg/380px-Homeless_woman_sitting.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Homeless_woman_sitting.jpg/506px-Homeless_woman_sitting.jpg 2x" width="253"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Homeless_woman_sitting.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A woman sitting on steps with a broken shopping cart full of papers to the left. Around her there is trash and the floor looks dirty and unsanitary.</div></div></div>
<p>Mental illness is thought to be highly prevalent among homeless populations, though access to proper diagnoses is limited. An article written by Lisa Goodman and her colleagues summarized Smith's research into PTSD in homeless single women and mothers in St. Louis, Missouri, which found that 53% of the respondents met diagnostic criteria, and which describes homelessness as a risk factor for mental illness.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Homelessness_as_psychological_traum_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-Homelessness_as_psychological_traum-53">[53]</a></sup> At least two commonly reported symptoms of psychological trauma, social disaffiliation and learned helplessness are highly prevalent among homeless individuals and families.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hwang_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hwang-54">[54]</a></sup>
</p><p>While mental illness is prevalent, people infrequently receive appropriate care.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Homelessness_as_psychological_traum_53-1"><a href="#cite_note-Homelessness_as_psychological_traum-53">[53]</a></sup> Case management linked to other services is an effective care approach for improving symptoms in people experiencing homelessness.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hwang_54-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hwang-54">[54]</a></sup> Case management reduced admission to hospitals, and it reduced substance use by those with substance abuse problems more than typical care.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hwang_54-2"><a href="#cite_note-Hwang-54">[54]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Immigrants_and_refugees">Immigrants and refugees</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mental_health&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Immigrants and refugees">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mental_health_of_refugees" title="Mental health of refugees">Mental health of refugees</a></div>
<p>States that produce refugees are sites of social upheaval, civil war, even genocide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:7_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-:7-55">[55]</a></sup> Most refugees experience trauma. It can be in the form of torture, sexual assault, family fragmentation, and death of loved ones.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:7_55-1"><a href="#cite_note-:7-55">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:8_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-:8-56">[56]</a></sup>
</p><p>Refugees and immigrants experience psychosocial stressors after resettlement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:9_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-:9-57">[57]</a></sup> These include discrimination, lack of economic stability, and social isolation causing emotional distress.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:7_55-2"><a href="#cite_note-:7-55">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:8_56-1"><a href="#cite_note-:8-56">[56]</a></sup> For refugees family reunification can be one of the primary needs to improve quality of life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:7_55-3"><a href="#cite_note-:7-55">[55]</a></sup> Post-migration trauma is a cause of depressive disorders and psychological distress for immigrants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:7_55-4"><a href="#cite_note-:7-55">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:8_56-2"><a href="#cite_note-:8-56">[56]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:9_57-1"><a href="#cite_note-:9-57">[57]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_and_religious_considerations">Cultural and religious considerations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mental_health&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Cultural and religious considerations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Mental health is a socially constructed concept; different societies, groups, <a href="/wiki/Culture" title="Culture">cultures</a>, institutions, and professions have very different ways of conceptualizing its nature and causes, determining what is mentally healthy, and deciding what interventions, if any, are appropriate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weare2000_p12_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-Weare2000_p12-58">[58]</a></sup> Thus, different professionals will have different cultural, class, political and religious backgrounds, which will impact the <a href="/wiki/Methodology" title="Methodology">methodology</a> applied during treatment. In the context of <a href="/wiki/Deaf_mental_health_care" title="Deaf mental health care">deaf mental health care</a>, it is necessary for professionals to have cultural competency of deaf and hard of hearing people and to understand how to properly rely on trained, qualified, and certified interpreters when working with <a href="/wiki/Deaf_culture" title="Deaf culture">culturally Deaf</a> clients.
</p><p>Research has shown that there is <a href="/wiki/Social_stigma" title="Social stigma">stigma</a> attached to mental illness.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> Due to such stigma, individuals may resist labeling and may be driven to respond to mental health diagnoses with <a href="/wiki/Denialism" title="Denialism">denialism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> Family caregivers of individuals with mental disorders may also suffer discrimination or face stigma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup>
</p><p>Addressing and eliminating the social stigma and <a href="/wiki/Treatment_of_mental_disorders" title="Treatment of mental disorders">perceived stigma</a> attached to mental illness has been recognized as crucial to education and awareness surrounding mental health issues. In the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Royal_College_of_Psychiatrists" title="Royal College of Psychiatrists">Royal College of Psychiatrists</a> organized the campaign <i>Changing Minds</i> (1998–2003) to help reduce stigma,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> while in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, efforts by entities such as the <a href="/wiki/Born_This_Way_Foundation" title="Born This Way Foundation">Born This Way Foundation</a> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Manic_Monologues" title="The Manic Monologues">The Manic Monologues</a></i> specifically focus on removing the stigma surrounding mental illness.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WaPo-stigma_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-WaPo-stigma-63">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KQED-stigma_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-KQED-stigma-64">[64]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/National_Alliance_on_Mental_Illness" title="National Alliance on Mental Illness">National Alliance on Mental Illness</a> (NAMI) is a U.S. institution founded in 1979 to represent and advocate for those struggling with mental health issues. NAMI helps to educate about mental illnesses and health issues, while also working to eliminate stigma<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> attached to these disorders.
</p><p>Many <a href="/wiki/Mental_health_professional" title="Mental health professional">mental health professionals</a> are beginning to, or already understand, the importance of competency in religious diversity and <a href="/wiki/Spirituality" title="Spirituality">spirituality</a>. They are also partaking in cultural training to better understand which interventions work best for these different groups of people. The <a href="/wiki/American_Psychological_Association" title="American Psychological Association">American Psychological Association</a> explicitly states that <a href="/wiki/Religion" title="Religion">religion</a> must be respected. Education in <a href="/wiki/Spirituality" title="Spirituality">spiritual</a> and religious matters is also required by the <a href="/wiki/American_Psychiatric_Association" title="American Psychiatric Association">American Psychiatric Association</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HandbookofPsychotherapyandReligousDiversity_p4_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-HandbookofPsychotherapyandReligousDiversity_p4-66">[66]</a></sup> however, far less attention is paid to the damage that more rigid, fundamentalist faiths commonly practiced in the United States can cause.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Reliable sources"><span title='The material near this tag may rely on an unreliable source. Using this for this statement is akin to using an anti-vax site to claim that not enough attention is paid to "vaccination injury" (June 2022)'>unreliable source?</span></a></i>]</sup> This theme has been widely politicized in 2018 such as with the creation of the Religious Liberty Task Force in July of that year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> Also, many providers and practitioners in the United States are only beginning to realize that the institution of mental healthcare lacks knowledge and competence of many non-Western cultures, leaving providers in the United States ill-equipped to treat patients from different cultures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Occupations">Occupations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mental_health&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Occupations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Mental_health_in_aviation" title="Mental health in aviation">Mental health in aviation</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Occupational_therapy">Occupational therapy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mental_health&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Occupational therapy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Occupational_therapy" title="Occupational therapy">Occupational therapy</a> practitioners aim to improve and enable a client or group’s participation in meaningful, everyday occupations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> In this sense, occupation is defined as any activity that “occupies one's time". Examples of those activities include daily tasks (dressing, bathing, eating, house chores, driving, etc.), sleep and rest, education, work, play, leisure (hobbies), and social interactions. The OT profession offers a vast range of services for all stages of life in a myriad of practice settings, though the foundations of OT come from mental health.
</p><p>OT services focused on mental health can be provided to persons, groups, and populations <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> across the lifespan and experiencing varying levels of mental health performance. For example, occupational therapy practitioners provide mental health services in school systems, military environments, hospitals, outpatient clinics, and inpatient mental health rehabilitation settings. Interventions or support can be provided directly through specific treatment interventions or indirectly by providing consultation to businesses, schools, or other larger groups to incorporate mental health strategies on a programmatic level. Even people who are mentally healthy can benefit from the health promotion and additional prevention strategies to reduce the impact of difficult situations. 
</p><p>The interventions focus on positive functioning, sensory strategies, managing emotions, interpersonal relationships, sleep, community engagement, and other cognitive skills (i.e. visual-perceptual skills, attention, memory, arousal/energy management, etc.).
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mental_health_in_social_work"><span class="anchor" id="Psychiatric_social_work"></span>Mental health in social work</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mental_health&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Mental health in social work">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Social_work" title="Social work">Social work</a></div><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Clinical_social_work" title="Clinical social work">Clinical social work</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Social_work" title="Social work">Social work</a> in mental health, also called psychiatric social work, is a process where an individual in a setting is helped to attain freedom from overlapping internal and external problems (social and economic situations, family and other relationships, the physical and organizational environment, psychiatric symptoms, etc.). It aims for harmony, <a href="/wiki/Quality_of_life" title="Quality of life">quality of life</a>, self-actualization and personal adaptation across all systems. Psychiatric social workers are <a href="/wiki/Mental_health_professional" title="Mental health professional">mental health professionals</a> that can assist patients and their family members in coping with both mental health issues and various economic or social problems caused by mental illness or psychiatric dysfunctions and to attain improved mental health and well-being. They are vital members of the treatment teams in Departments of Psychiatry and Behavioral Sciences in hospitals. They are employed in both outpatient and inpatient settings of a hospital, nursing homes, state and local governments, substance use clinics, correctional facilities, health care services, private practice, etc.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the United States, social workers provide most of the mental health services. According to government sources, 60 percent of mental health professionals are <a href="/wiki/Clinical_social_work" title="Clinical social work">clinically trained social workers</a>, 10 percent are <a href="/wiki/Psychiatrist" title="Psychiatrist">psychiatrists</a>, 23 percent are <a href="/wiki/Psychologist" title="Psychologist">psychologists</a>, and 5 percent are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Psychiatric_nurse" title="Psychiatric nurse">psychiatric nurses</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup>
</p><p>Mental health social workers in Japan have professional knowledge of health and welfare and skills essential for person's well-being. Their social work training enables them as a professional to carry out Consultation assistance for mental disabilities and their social reintegration; Consultation regarding the rehabilitation of the victims; Advice and guidance for post-discharge residence and re-employment after hospitalized care, for major life events in regular life, money and self-management and other relevant matters to equip them to adapt in daily life. Social workers provide individual home visits for mentally ill and do welfare services available, with specialized training a range of procedural services are coordinated for home, workplace and school. In an administrative relationship, Psychiatric social workers provides consultation, leadership, conflict management and work direction. Psychiatric social workers who provides assessment and psychosocial interventions function as a clinician, counselor and municipal staff of the health centers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Causing_Factors_for_Mental_Health_Problems">Causing Factors for Mental Health Problems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mental_health&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Causing Factors for Mental Health Problems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>There are many factors that contribute to mental health problems including; biological, such as genes or brain chemistry, life experiences, such as trauma or abuse, and family history of mental health problems.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> Factors affecting or contributing to the mental health of an individual.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_factors">Economic factors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mental_health&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Economic factors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Socioeconomic_status_and_mental_health" title="Socioeconomic status and mental health">Socioeconomic status and mental health</a></div>
<p>Unemployment has been shown to hurt an individual's emotional well-being, <a href="/wiki/Self-esteem" title="Self-esteem">self-esteem</a>, and more broadly their mental health. Increasing unemployment has been shown to have a significant impact on mental health, predominantly depressive disorders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> This is an important consideration when reviewing the triggers for mental health disorders in any population survey.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:277px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_prevalence_of_mental_illness_is_higher_in_more_unequal_rich_countries.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="734" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="197" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/The_prevalence_of_mental_illness_is_higher_in_more_unequal_rich_countries.jpg/275px-The_prevalence_of_mental_illness_is_higher_in_more_unequal_rich_countries.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/The_prevalence_of_mental_illness_is_higher_in_more_unequal_rich_countries.jpg/413px-The_prevalence_of_mental_illness_is_higher_in_more_unequal_rich_countries.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/The_prevalence_of_mental_illness_is_higher_in_more_unequal_rich_countries.jpg/550px-The_prevalence_of_mental_illness_is_higher_in_more_unequal_rich_countries.jpg 2x" width="275"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_prevalence_of_mental_illness_is_higher_in_more_unequal_rich_countries.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The prevalence of mental illness is higher in more <a href="/wiki/Economic_inequality" title="Economic inequality">unequal</a> rich countries.</div></div></div><p>Emotional mental disorders are a leading cause of disabilities worldwide. Investigating the degree and severity of untreated emotional mental disorders throughout the world is a top priority of the <a href="/wiki/World_Mental_Health_survey_initiative" title="World Mental Health survey initiative">World Mental Health</a> (WMH) survey initiative,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> which was created in 1998 by the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> (WHO).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neuropsychiatric" title="Neuropsychiatric">Neuropsychiatric</a> disorders are the leading causes of disability worldwide, accounting for 37% of all healthy life years lost through disease. These disorders are most destructive to low and middle-income countries due to their inability to provide their citizens with proper aid. Despite modern treatment and rehabilitation for emotional mental health disorders, "even economically advantaged societies have competing priorities and budgetary constraints".
</p><p>The World Mental Health survey initiative has suggested a plan for countries to redesign their mental health care systems to best allocate resources.
"A first step is documentation of services being used and the extent and nature of unmet treatment needs. A second step could be to do a cross-national comparison of service use and unmet needs in countries with different mental health care systems. Such comparisons can help to uncover optimum financing, national policies, and delivery systems for mental health care."<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Inline_citation#When_you_must_use_inline_citations" title="Wikipedia:Inline citation"><span title="The text near this tag needs a citation. (October 2020)">quote citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>Knowledge of how to provide effective emotional mental health care has become imperative worldwide. Unfortunately, most countries have insufficient data to guide decisions, absent or competing visions for resources, and near-constant pressures to cut insurance and entitlements. WMH surveys were done in Africa (<a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a>, South Africa), the Americas (Colombia, Mexico, United States), Asia and the Pacific (<a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shanghai" title="Shanghai">Shanghai</a> in the <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">People's Republic of China</a>), Europe (Belgium, France, Germany, Italy, Netherlands, Spain, Ukraine), and the middle east (Israel, Lebanon). Countries were classified with <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> criteria as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Low_income" title="Low income">low-income</a> (<a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a>), lower-middle-income (<a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>), higher middle-income (<a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>), and high-income.
</p><p>The coordinated surveys on emotional mental health disorders, their severity, and treatments were implemented in the aforementioned countries. These surveys assessed the frequency, types, and adequacy of mental health service use in 17 countries in which WMH surveys are complete. The WMH also examined unmet needs for treatment in strata defined by the seriousness of mental disorders. Their research showed that "the number of respondents using any 12-month mental health service was generally lower in developing than in developed countries, and the proportion receiving services tended to correspond to countries' percentages of <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">gross domestic product</a> spent on health care".
"High levels of unmet need worldwide are not surprising, since WHO Project <a href="/wiki/ATLAS_experiment" title="ATLAS experiment">ATLAS</a>' findings of much lower mental health expenditures than was suggested by the magnitude of burdens from mental illnesses. Generally, unmet needs in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Low-income" title="Low-income">low-income</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Middle-income" title="Middle-income">middle-income</a> countries might be attributable to these nations spending reduced amounts (usually &lt;1%) of already diminished health budgets on mental health care, and they rely heavily on out-of-pocket spending by citizens who are ill-equipped for it".
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Stress">Stress</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mental_health&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Stress">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Centre_for_Addiction_and_Mental_Health" title="Centre for Addiction and Mental Health">Centre for Addiction and Mental Health</a> discuss how a certain amount of stress is a normal part of daily life. Small doses of stress help people meet deadlines, be prepared for presentations, be productive and arrive on time for important events. However, long-term stress can become harmful. When stress becomes overwhelming and prolonged, the risks for mental health problems and medical problems increase."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> Also on that note, some studies have found language to deteriorate mental health and even harm humans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_factor">Cultural factor</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mental_health&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Cultural factor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There are significant variations in the cultural views of mental illness across cultures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> Culture influences the epidemiology, phenomenology, outcome, and treatment of mental illness.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> Culture has multiple roles to play in the expression of psychopathological disorder.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Protection_and_promotion">Protection and promotion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mental_health&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Protection and promotion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Prevention_of_mental_disorders" title="Prevention of mental disorders">Prevention of mental disorders</a></div>
<p>"The terms mental health promotion and prevention have often been confused. Promotion is defined as intervening to <i>optimize</i> positive mental health by addressing determinants of positive mental health (i.e. <a href="/wiki/Protective_factor" title="Protective factor">protective factors</a>) before a specific mental health problem has been identified, with the ultimate goal of improving the positive mental health of the population. Mental health prevention is defined as intervening to <i>minimize</i> mental health problems (i.e. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Risk_factors" title="Risk factors">risk factors</a>) by addressing determinants of mental health problems before a specific mental health problem has been identified in the individual, group, or population of focus with the ultimate goal of reducing the number of future mental health problems in the population."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MHPPYouth_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-MHPPYouth-85">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup>
</p><p>In order to improve mental health, the root of the issue has to be resolved. "Prevention emphasizes the avoidance of risk factors; promotion aims to enhance an individual's ability to achieve a positive sense of <a href="/wiki/Self-esteem" title="Self-esteem">self-esteem</a>, mastery, well-being, and social inclusion."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> Mental health promotion attempts to increase protective factors and healthy behaviors that can help prevent the onset of a diagnosable mental disorder and reduce risk factors that can lead to the development of a mental disorder.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MHPPYouth_85-1"><a href="#cite_note-MHPPYouth-85">[85]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Yoga" title="Yoga">Yoga</a> is an example of an activity that calms one's entire body and nerves.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> According to a study on well-being by Richards, Campania, and Muse-Burke, "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mindfulness_(psychology)" title="Mindfulness (psychology)">mindfulness</a> is considered to be a purposeful state, it may be that those who practice it belief in its importance and value being mindful, so that valuing of self-care activities may influence the intentional component of mindfulness."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Richards_2010_247_36-3"><a href="#cite_note-Richards_2010_247-36">[36]</a></sup>
</p><p>Mental health is conventionally defined as a hybrid of the absence of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mental_disorders" title="Mental disorders">mental disorder</a> and the presence of well-being. Focus is increasing on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mental_disorders#Prevention" title="Mental disorders">preventing mental disorders</a>.
Prevention is beginning to appear in mental health strategies, including the 2004 WHO report "<i>Prevention of Mental Disorders</i>", the 2008 EU "Pact for Mental Health" and the 2011 US National Prevention Strategy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-89">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (January 2016)">page needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Some commentators have argued that a pragmatic and practical approach to mental disorder prevention at work would be to treat it the same way as physical injury prevention.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup>
</p><p>Prevention of a disorder at a young age may significantly decrease the chances that a child will have a disorder later in life, and shall be the most efficient and effective measure from a public health perspective.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> Prevention may require the regular consultation of a <a href="/wiki/Physician" title="Physician">physician</a> for at least twice a year to detect any signs that reveal any mental health concerns.
</p><p>Additionally, social media is becoming a resource for prevention. In 2004, the Mental Health Services Act<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> began to fund marketing initiatives to educate the public on mental health. This California-based project is working to combat the negative perception with mental health and reduce the stigma associated with it. While social media can benefit mental health, it can also lead to deterioration if not managed properly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> Limiting social media intake is beneficial.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup>
</p><p>Studies report that patients in mental health care who can access and read their <a href="/wiki/Electronic_health_record" title="Electronic health record">Electronic Health Records</a> (EHR) or <a href="/wiki/OpenNotes" title="OpenNotes">Open Notes</a> online experience increased understanding of their mental health, feeling in control of their care, and enhanced trust in their clinicians. Patients' also reported feelings of greater validation, engagement, remembering their care plan, and acquiring a better awareness of potential <a href="/wiki/Side_effect" title="Side effect">side effects</a> of their <a href="/wiki/Medication" title="Medication">medications</a>, when reading their mental health notes. Other common experiences were that shared mental health notes enhance <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Patient_empowerment" title="Patient empowerment">patient empowerment</a> and augment <a href="/wiki/Autonomy" title="Autonomy">patient autonomy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Care_navigation">Care navigation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mental_health&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Care navigation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mental_health_care_navigator" title="Mental health care navigator">Mental health care navigator</a></div>
<p>Mental health care navigation helps to guide patients and families through the fragmented, often confusing mental health industries. Care navigators work closely with patients and families through discussion and collaboration to provide information on best therapies as well as referrals to practitioners and facilities specializing in particular forms of emotional improvement. The difference between therapy and care navigation is that the care navigation process provides information and directs patients to therapy rather than providing therapy. Still, care navigators may offer diagnosis and treatment planning. Though many care navigators are also trained therapists and doctors. Care navigation is the link between the patient and the below therapies. A clear recognition that mental health requires medical intervention was demonstrated in a study by Kessler et al. of the prevalence and treatment of mental disorders from 1990 to 2003 in the United States. Despite the prevalence of mental health disorders remaining unchanged during this period, the number of patients seeking treatment for mental disorders increased threefold.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Methods">Methods</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mental_health&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Methods">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Pharmacotherapy">Pharmacotherapy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mental_health&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Pharmacotherapy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Pharmacotherapy" title="Pharmacotherapy">Pharmacotherapy</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Therapy" title="Therapy">therapy</a> that uses pharmaceutical drugs. Pharmacotherapy is used in the treatment of mental illness through the use of <a href="/wiki/Antidepressant" title="Antidepressant">antidepressants</a>, <a href="/wiki/Benzodiazepine" title="Benzodiazepine">benzodiazepines</a>, and the use of elements such as <a href="/wiki/Lithium_(medication)" title="Lithium (medication)">lithium</a>. It can only be prescribed by a medical professional trained in the field of <a href="/wiki/Psychiatry" title="Psychiatry">Psychiatry</a>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Physical_activity">Physical activity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mental_health&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Physical activity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Exercise" title="Exercise">Physical exercise</a> can improve mental and physical health. Playing sports, walking, cycling, or doing any form of physical activity trigger the production of various hormones, sometimes including endorphins, which can elevate a person's mood.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup>
</p><p>Studies have shown that in some cases, physical activity can have the same impact as antidepressants when treating depression and anxiety.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup>
</p><p>Moreover, cessation of physical exercise may have adverse effects on some mental health conditions, such as depression and anxiety. This could lead to different negative outcomes such as obesity, skewed body image and many health risks associated with mental illnesses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup>Exercise can improve mental health but it should not be used as an alternative to therapy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Activity_therapies">Activity therapies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mental_health&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Activity therapies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Activity therapies also called recreation therapy and occupational therapy, promote healing through active engagement. An example of occupational therapy would be promoting an activity that improves daily life, such as self-care or improving hobbies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> Similarly, recreational therapy focuses on movement, such as walking, yoga, or riding a bike.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup>
</p><p>Each of these therapies have proven to improve mental health and have resulted in healthier, happier individuals. In recent years, for example, coloring has been recognized as an activity that has been proven to significantly lower the levels of depressive symptoms and anxiety in many studies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Expressive_therapies">Expressive therapies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mental_health&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Expressive therapies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Expressive_therapies" title="Expressive therapies">Expressive therapies</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Creative_arts_therapies" title="Creative arts therapies">creative arts therapies</a> are a form of <a href="/wiki/Psychotherapy" title="Psychotherapy">psychotherapy</a> that involves the arts or art-making. These therapies include <a href="/wiki/Art_therapy" title="Art therapy">art therapy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Music_therapy" title="Music therapy">music therapy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Drama_therapy" title="Drama therapy">drama therapy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dance_therapy" title="Dance therapy">dance therapy</a>, and poetry therapy. It has been proven that music therapy is an effective way of helping people with a mental health disorder.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> Drama therapy is approved by NICE for the treatment of psychosis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Psychotherapy">Psychotherapy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mental_health&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Psychotherapy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Psychotherapy" title="Psychotherapy">Psychotherapy</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Psychotherapy" title="Psychotherapy">Psychotherapy</a> is the general term for the scientific based treatment of mental health issues based on modern medicine. It includes a number of schools, such as <a href="/wiki/Gestalt_therapy" title="Gestalt therapy">gestalt therapy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Psychoanalysis" title="Psychoanalysis">psychoanalysis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cognitive_behavioral_therapy" title="Cognitive behavioral therapy">cognitive behavioral therapy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Psychedelic_therapy" title="Psychedelic therapy">psychedelic therapy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Transpersonal_psychology" title="Transpersonal psychology">transpersonal psychology</a>/psychotherapy, and <a href="/wiki/Dialectical_behavior_therapy" title="Dialectical behavior therapy">dialectical behavioral therapy</a>.
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Group_therapy" title="Group therapy">Group therapy</a> involves any type of therapy that takes place in a setting involving multiple people. It can include <a href="/wiki/Psychodynamic_psychotherapy" title="Psychodynamic psychotherapy">psychodynamic</a> groups, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Expressive_therapy" title="Expressive therapy">expressive therapy</a> groups, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Support_groups" title="Support groups">support groups</a> (including the <a href="/wiki/Twelve-step_program" title="Twelve-step program">Twelve-step program</a>), problem-solving and <a href="/wiki/Psychoeducation" title="Psychoeducation">psychoeducation</a> groups.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Self-compassion">Self-compassion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mental_health&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Self-compassion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Self-compassion" title="Self-compassion">Self-compassion</a></div>
<p>According to Neff, self-compassion consists of three main positive components and their negative counterparts: Self-Kindness versus Self-Judgement, Common Humanity versus Isolation and Mindfulness versus Over-Identification.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> Furthermore, there is evidence from a study by Shin &amp; Lin suggesting specific components of self-compassion can predict specific dimensions of positive mental health (emotional, social, and psychological well-being).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Social-emotional_learning">Social-emotional learning</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mental_health&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Social-emotional learning">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Social_emotional_development#Social_emotional_learning_&amp;_development_in_schools" title="Social emotional development">Social emotional development § Social emotional learning &amp; development in schools</a></div>
<p>The Collaborative for academic, social, emotional learning (CASEL) addresses five broad and interrelated areas of competence and highlights examples for each: self-awareness, self-management, social awareness, relationship skills,<i> and </i>responsible decision-making.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> A meta-analysis was done by Alexendru Boncu, Iuliana Costeau, &amp; Mihaela Minulescu (2017) looking at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Social-emotional_learning" title="Social-emotional learning">social-emotional learning</a> (SEL) studies and the effects on emotional and behavior outcomes. They found a small but significant effect size (across the studies looked into) for externalized problems and social-emotional skills.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup>
</p>
